###xml 860 861 856 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
###xml 903 933 899 929 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Castillo-Davis1">Castillo-Davis and Hartl (2002</xref>
###xml 1044 1045 1040 1041 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sub>
###xml 584 594 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The KA/KS ratio, a measure of selective pressure, is expected to be 1.0 for genes that are under no selective pressure (for example, pseudogenes), less than 1.0 for genes under purifying selection, and greater than 1.0 for genes under positive selection. As expected, we found that nearly all the genes in ortholog pairs are under purifying selection (Figure 2). However, the extent of this purifying selection is more marked in genes with essential functions. For example, ortholog pairs which exhibit an embryonic lethal phenotype in systematic RNA inhibition (RNAi) screens of the C. elegans ortholog partner (Maeda et al. 2001; Piano and Gunsalus 2002; Kamath et al. 2003) show a markedly lower KA/KS ratio than do pairs for which a wild-type phenotype was observed (KA/KS, 0.0445 +/- 0.0340 versus 0.0627 +/- 0.0494; p < 1 x 10-16 by the Welch two-sample t-test). We also confirmed the findings of Castillo-Davis and Hartl (2002), who showed that genes involved early in development tend to be less prone to duplications and have a lower KS value than late-development genes (data not shown).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 151 170 151 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Jordan1">Jordan et al. (2002</xref>
###xml 271 287 271 287 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Escherichia coli</named-content>
###xml 289 308 289 308 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Helicobacter pylori</named-content>
###xml 314 336 314 336 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Neisseria meningitidis</named-content>
###xml 271 287 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 289 308 <span type="species:ncbi:210">Helicobacter pylori</span>
###xml 314 336 <span type="species:ncbi:487">Neisseria meningitidis</span>
The trend towards higher levels of purifying selection in essential genes has been seen in organisms as distantly related as prokaryotes. For example, Jordan et al. (2002) found similar differences when comparing rates of evolution of essential and nonessential genes in Escherichia coli, Helicobacter pylori, and Neisseria meningitidis.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 62 85 62 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Civetta1">Civetta and Singh (1998</xref>
###xml 114 115 114 115 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sub>
###xml 117 118 117 118 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sub>
###xml 154 159 154 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-1</italic>
###xml 164 169 164 169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">tra-2</italic>
###xml 342 343 342 343 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sub>
###xml 345 346 345 346 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</sub>
###xml 1036 1052 1036 1052 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Yang2">Yang et al. 2000</xref>
We also looked for genes with evidence of positive selection. Civetta and Singh (1998) reported generally higher KA/KS ratios for sex determination genes tra-1 and tra-2 than for other sampled genes and interpreted this as positive selection on genes that are involved in speciation. Under the strict definition of positive selection, where KA/KS > 1.0, we do not find evidence for positive selection in these genes, but given the high value of substitution between the two species, genes with a ratio greater than 1.0 may no longer be recognizable as orthologs. Perhaps genes under positive selection might be found among members of gene families or in genes that are no longer recognizably similar at the primary sequence level. Sequence analysis of species of intermediate evolutionary distance, if available, would be revealing. Also, since our tests for positive selection are very conservative, we would not detect any sites under positive selection if they are small in proportion to those of the gene under purifying selection (Yang et al. 2000).
###end p 65
###begin title 66
###xml 15 26 15 26 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 27 37 27 37 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 15 26 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 27 37 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Estimating the C. briggsae/C. elegans Divergence Date 
###end title 66
###begin p 67
###xml 73 85 73 85 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Blaxter1">Blaxter 1998</xref>
###xml 138 160 138 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 226 236 226 236 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 276 287 276 287 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 289 299 289 299 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">A. gambiae</named-content>
###xml 305 315 305 315 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">H. sapiens</named-content>
###xml 421 443 421 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 138 149 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 150 160 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 226 236 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 276 287 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 289 299 <span type="species:ncbi:7165">A. gambiae</span>
###xml 305 315 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">H. sapiens</span>
###xml 421 432 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 433 443 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Using the divergence of the nematodes from the arthropods 800-1,000 MYA (Blaxter 1998) to calibrate the molecular clock, we estimated the C. briggsae/C. elegans divergence date from 338 sets of orthologs. Each set comprised a C. elegans gene and its one-to-one orthologs from C. briggsae, A. gambiae, and H. sapiens. When the nematode/arthropod divergence is taken to be 800 MYA, a 95% confidence interval for the median C. briggsae/C. elegans speciation date is 78-90 MYA. If the nematode/arthropod divergence is taken to be 1,000 MYA, the interval becomes 97-113 MYA.
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 25 47 25 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 234 245 234 245 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 254 276 254 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Coghlan1">Coghlan and Wolfe 2002</xref>
###xml 372 383 372 383 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 503 524 503 524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Waterston1">Waterston et al. 2002</xref>
###xml 546 568 546 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 25 36 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 37 47 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 234 245 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 372 383 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 466 471 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 472 477 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 546 557 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 558 568 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Our best estimate of the C. briggsae/C. elegans speciation date is therefore approximately 80-110 MYA. This confidence interval is tighter than a previous estimate of 50-120 MYA made using 92 sets of orthologs from the then available C. briggsae genome (Coghlan and Wolfe 2002). The current estimate is probably more accurate due to both a larger sample size and improved C. briggsae gene predictions and ortholog assignments. Interestingly, recent studies date the mouse/human divergence to 65-75 MYA (Waterston et al. 2002), so the date of the C. briggsae/C. elegans divergence was between 5 and 45 MY before the rodent/primate divergence.
###end p 68
###begin title 69
###xml 0 11 0 11 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 12 22 12 22 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 0 11 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 12 22 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
C. briggsae/C. elegans Paralogs and Orphans
###end title 69
###begin p 70
###xml 49 60 49 60 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 100 110 100 110 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 146 156 146 156 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 161 172 161 172 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 229 239 229 239 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 270 281 270 281 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 49 60 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 100 110 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 146 156 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 161 172 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 229 239 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 270 281 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
In this section, we look in more detail at those C. briggsae proteins that could not be assigned to C. elegans orthologs. Roughly, a third of the C. elegans and C. briggsae proteins fall into this category. Of these, 4,545 (23%) C. elegans (WS77*) genes and 5,211 (28%) C. briggsae proteins have multiple BLASTP matches in the opposite species. These correspond to paralogous relationships within gene families and are examined in greater detail in the next section (Gene Families).
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 26 36 26 36 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 53 64 53 64 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 101 102 101 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 112 115 112 115 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;10</sup>
###xml 311 312 311 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 322 324 322 324 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 335 346 335 346 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 373 383 373 383 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 452 462 452 462 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 501 511 501 511 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 629 640 629 640 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 687 709 687 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 26 36 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 53 64 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 335 346 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 373 383 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 452 462 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 501 511 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 629 640 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 687 698 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 699 709 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The remaining 2,108 (11%) C. elegans and 2,141 (11%) C. briggsae genes do not have any BLASTP hit of E-value <10-10 in the opposite genome and therefore represent candidate species-specific genes, or "orphans." However, many of these are simply genes that have evolved rapidly. Lowering the BLASTP threshold to E-value <10-5 finds 785 C. briggsae proteins that have a weak C. elegans match. An additional 11 proteins have a strong TBLASTN match to the C. elegans genomic sequence, signifying either a C. elegans gene that is missing from the predicted gene set or a pseudogene. These are being examined individually. Another 538 C. briggsae genes were found by TRIBE to belong to shared C. briggsae/C. elegans gene families (see the Gene Families section below) and so are members of rapidly evolving families common to both species.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 16 27 16 27 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 64 66 64 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E-</italic>
###xml 76 78 76 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 139 161 139 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 207 217 207 217 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 241 252 241 252 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 267 277 267 277 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 404 414 404 414 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 16 27 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 139 150 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 151 161 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 207 217 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 241 252 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 267 277 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 404 414 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
This leaves 807 C. briggsae proteins that have no BLASTP match (E-value, <10-5) in the opposite species and that do not belong to a shared C. briggsae/C. elegans gene family. A similar analysis yields 1,061 C. elegans orphans. Of these, 695 C. briggsae genes and 963 C. elegans genes have at least two exons and so are less likely than single-exon predictions to be pseudogenes or mispredictions. Of the C. elegans orphans, 208 (22%) have partial or full empirical confirmation of their gene structures in the form of ESTs or cDNA data.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 120 129 120 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Long1">Long 2001</xref>
Some of these orphans may be novel genes that have been generated in one of the two genomes since the species diverged (Long 2001). However, we emphasize that some of the candidate orphans may not be real orphans at all, but are either pseudogenes that have not yet been deleted or are very rapidly evolving genes that have diverged so quickly that the BLAST and Smith-Waterman algorithms (used in the Gene Families section) cannot recognize their cross-species matches. In either case, it will be fruitful to look at the orphans in more detail because they are likely to reveal sites of rapid evolution.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 48 58 48 58 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="sd003">Dataset S3</xref>
A list of the candidate orphans is available as Dataset S3.
###end p 74
###begin title 75
Protein Families
###end title 75
###begin p 76
###xml 49 60 49 60 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 121 131 121 131 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 136 147 136 147 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 194 217 194 217 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Smith1">Smith and Waterman 1981</xref>
###xml 246 257 246 257 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 262 272 262 272 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 406 425 406 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Enright1">Enright et al. 2002</xref>
###xml 524 535 524 535 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 540 550 540 550 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 49 60 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 121 131 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 136 147 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 246 257 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 262 272 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 524 535 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 540 550 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
In order to identify protein family structure in C. briggsae while simultaneously identifying conserved families in both C. elegans and C. briggsae, we performed all-against-all Smith-Waterman (Smith and Waterman 1981) alignments of the combined C. briggsae and C. elegans (WS77*) predicted protein sets. The pairwise protein similarity data were then used to cluster proteins with the TRIBE-MCL software (Enright et al. 2002). To characterize the clusters, we correlated clusters with the protein family domain analysis of C. briggsae and C. elegans proteins described earlier and kept the domain descriptions that were held in common by the majority of cluster members.
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 535 545 535 545 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 550 561 550 561 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 584 591 584 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio.0000045-t003">Table 3</xref>
###xml 535 545 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 550 561 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The TRIBE-MCL analysis produced 7,778 clusters, 2,169 of which contained more than two genes. The largest cluster contained 775 genes with a eukaryotic protein kinase protein domain. The next largest clusters were associated with Zn finger, C4-type steroid receptor and ligand-binding domain of nuclear hormone receptor, 7TM receptors, and EGF-like domain. We found 852 clusters of more than two genes (comprising 4,567 genes in total) contained no identifiable Pfam domains. The top ten largest gene families with their percentage of C. elegans and C. briggsae proteins are shown in Table 3.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 72 82 72 82 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 87 98 87 98 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 234 245 234 245 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 355 365 355 365 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 660 682 660 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 72 82 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 87 98 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 234 245 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 355 365 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 660 671 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 672 682 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
While the great majority of TRIBE-MCL clusters had a balanced number of C. elegans and C. briggsae members, we found several interesting exceptions. For clusters of more than two proteins, a total of 328 clusters were made up of only C. briggsae genes; 283 of these did not have identifiable Pfam domains. Similarly there were 111 clusters that contained C. elegans proteins exclusively, 98 of which had no identifiable Pfam domains. Although some of these putative families are undoubtedly artifacts from the gene-calling procedure, some may be true species-specific families, at least at the limit of the sequence similarity criteria used here (see also the C. briggsae/C. elegans Paralogs and Orphans section above).
###end p 78
###begin p 79
###xml 238 248 238 248 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 371 382 371 382 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 583 593 583 593 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 604 615 604 615 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 778 789 778 789 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 824 834 824 834 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 917 928 917 928 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 943 953 943 953 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 238 248 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 371 382 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 583 593 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 604 615 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 778 789 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 824 834 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 917 928 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 943 953 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
In other cases, a well-known gene family was found to have greater representation in one species than the other. A prominent example is the chemosensory receptor (also known as the olfactory receptor) family. While there are 718 putative C. elegans chemosensory receptor proteins annotated in WS77*, the TRIBE-MCL clustering and Pfam annotation detects only 429 putative C. briggsae chemosensory receptor proteins. Another example is a large family containing a cyclin-like F-box (usually associated with phosphorylation-dependent ubiquination) which is represented by 243 copies in C. elegans and 98 in C. briggsae. For clusters containing five or more members, there were 202 clusters with compositional differences of at least 2-fold between the two species (118 enriched in C. briggsae proteins, 84 clusters enriched in C. elegans proteins) and 12 clusters with compositional differences of at least 10-fold (ten C. briggsae-enriched; two C. elegans-enriched).
###end p 79
###begin p 80
###xml 60 79 60 79 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Bateman1">Bateman et al. 2002</xref>
###xml 415 422 415 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio.0000045-t004">Table 4</xref>
###xml 638 648 638 648 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 653 664 653 664 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 721 731 721 731 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 750 762 750 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae.</italic>
###xml 638 648 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 653 664 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 721 731 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 750 761 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The chemosensory receptor family is subdivided by Pfam 9.0 (Bateman et al. 2002) into six subfamilies: 7TM subfam4, 7TM subfam5, sra, srb, sre, and srg. To determine whether the difference in size of the chemosensory receptor families in the two species affects all subfamilies equally, we undertook a detailed analysis of the clusters using neighbor-joining trees and manual inspection. The results, summarized in Table 4, show that the size differential in the chemosensory receptor family between the two species is not distributed equally but is concentrated in two subfamilies: the 7TM subfam5 subfamily, with 311 and 151 members in C. elegans and C. briggsae respectively, and the sra subfamily, with 36 members in C. elegans and 18 members in C. briggsae.
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 0 8 0 8 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio.0000045-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 134 144 134 144 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 164 175 164 175 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 251 259 251 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio.0000045-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 280 290 280 290 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 392 402 392 402 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 414 426 414 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae.</italic>
###xml 467 478 467 478 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 134 144 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 164 175 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 280 290 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 392 402 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 414 425 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 467 478 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Figure 3 shows a phylogenetic tree for the sra subfamily. Many of the tree's terminal branches have exactly two members, one from the C. elegans and the other from C. briggsae. These cases correspond to putative orthologs. Several branches (arrows in Figure 3) show expansions in C. elegans that presumably represent cases in which a common ancestor in the two species underwent expansion in C. elegans but not in C. briggsae. A more modest expansion of a cluster of C. briggsae genes is also seen.
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 75 86 75 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans-</italic>
###xml 224 235 224 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans-</italic>
###xml 276 284 276 284 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio.0000045-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 358 368 358 368 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 392 400 392 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio.0000045-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 75 85 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 224 234 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 358 368 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
In the chemosensory receptor family, there is a strong correlation between C. elegans-specific expansions in the similarity tree and regions of tandem duplication in the genome. For example, all the genes found in the large C. elegans-specific expansion in the upper right of Figure 3 are tightly clustered in a tandem array within a single 20 kbp region of C. elegans chromosome I (inset of Figure 3, lower right).
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 71 81 71 81 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 83 120 83 120 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Celegans1">C. elegans Sequencing Consortium 1998</xref>
###xml 140 151 140 151 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 370 381 370 381 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 528 538 522 532 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 574 585 568 579 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 600 610 594 604 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 750 751 744 745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 71 81 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 83 93 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 140 151 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 370 381 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 528 538 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 574 585 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 600 610 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The physical clustering of protein families that was first observed in C. elegans (C. elegans Sequencing Consortium 1998) is also common in C. briggsae. To compare family clustering in the two species, we evaluated sliding windows of 15 protein-coding genes and determined the average number of gene products within the window that belonged to the same TRIBE family. In C. briggsae, the average (mean +/- SD) number of family members in a sliding window was 0.37 +/- 1.04, while a similar value of 0.55 +/- 1.57 was observed in C. elegans, in contrast to values of 0.00008 (C. briggsae) and 0.00058 (C. elegans) that are expected of families that are not clustered. A permutation test indicates that the relationship of families is highly nonrandom (p < 0.001) compared to a reshuffling of the genome on either a chromosome or a contig level.
###end p 83
###begin p 84
###xml 114 151 114 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Celegans1">C. elegans Sequencing Consortium 1998</xref>
###xml 153 167 153 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Gu2">Gu et al. 2002</xref>
###xml 169 193 169 193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Hughes1">Hughes and Friedman 2003</xref>
###xml 114 124 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The presumed mechanism for the observed clustering of family members is one or more cycles of tandem duplication (C. elegans Sequencing Consortium 1998; Gu et al. 2002; Hughes and Friedman 2003).
###end p 84
###begin title 85
Noncoding RNAs
###end title 85
###begin p 86
###xml 252 264 252 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae.</italic>
###xml 327 338 327 338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans.</italic>
###xml 252 263 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 327 337 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Noncoding RNAs (ncRNAs) are a class of gene that produce a functional transcript as a final product, rather than being translated into a protein. We used a combination of ncRNA prediction programs and similarity search algorithms to identify ncRNAs in C. briggsae. For the purposes of comparison, we repeated the analysis with C. elegans.
###end p 86
###begin p 87
###xml 28 39 28 39 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 63 73 63 73 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 75 82 75 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio.0000045-t005">Table 5</xref>
###xml 28 39 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 63 73 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We found 962 ncRNA genes in C. briggsae and 838 ncRNA genes in C. elegans (Table 5), as well as an additional 191 and 212 fragmentary matches in each species, respectively, that may be pseudogenes. Although the transfer RNA (tRNA) search software we used is able to distinguish pseudogenes from true genes with high sensitivity, this is not true of the other ncRNA assignments, which should therefore be treated with caution in the absence of experimental data.
###end p 87
###begin title 88
tRNA Genes
###end title 88
###begin p 89
###xml 64 75 64 75 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 87 97 87 97 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 190 227 190 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Celegans1">C. elegans Sequencing Consortium 1998</xref>
###xml 64 75 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 87 97 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 190 200 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We found 777 tRNA genes and 181 tRNA-derived pseudogenes in the C. briggsae genome. In C. elegans we found 609 tRNA genes and 210 tRNA pseudogenes, in good agreement with previous analyses (C. elegans Sequencing Consortium 1998).
###end p 89
###begin p 90
###xml 4 15 4 15 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 194 205 194 205 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 239 250 239 250 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 257 265 257 265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBG05747</italic>
###xml 285 295 285 295 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 301 308 301 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C06G3.7</italic>
###xml 382 402 382 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Buettner1">Buettner et al. 1999</xref>
###xml 4 15 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 194 205 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 239 250 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 285 295 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The C. briggsae tRNA set included two putative selenocysteine tRNAs. Furthermore we also identified a selenocysteine insertion sequence (SECIS) in the 3' untranslated region (UTR) of a putative C. briggsae thioredoxin reductase gene. This C. briggsae gene, CBG05747, is orthologous to C. elegans gene C06G3.7, and was previously reported to contain a conserved SECIS in the 3' UTR (Buettner et al. 1999).
###end p 90
###begin p 91
###xml 42 53 42 53 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 200 222 200 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 290 315 290 315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Guthrie1">Guthrie and Abelson (1982</xref>
###xml 353 406 353 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-International1">International Human Genome Sequencing Consortium 2001</xref>
###xml 42 53 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 200 211 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 212 222 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 339 344 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 367 372 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
The approximately 170 extra tRNA genes in C. briggsae are distributed across the amino acyl-tRNA families. We constructed neighbor-joining trees of the amino acyl-tRNA families and identified several C. briggsae/C. elegans orthologs (data not shown). The codon wobble patterns predicted by Guthrie and Abelson (1982) and described for the human genome (International Human Genome Sequencing Consortium 2001) are conserved in both nematodes.
###end p 91
###begin title 92
Ribosomal RNA Genes
###end title 92
###begin p 93
###xml 142 152 142 152 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 182 199 182 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Ellis1">Ellis et al. 1986</xref>
###xml 275 285 275 285 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 338 348 338 348 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 353 364 353 364 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 423 441 423 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Butler1">Butler et al. 1981</xref>
###xml 443 464 443 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Nelson1">Nelson and Honda 1989</xref>
###xml 543 554 543 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans.</italic>
###xml 142 152 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 275 285 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 338 348 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 353 364 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 543 553 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The genes for three of the four ribosomal RNA (rRNA) components, 18S, 5.8S, and 26S, are known to occur in large, tandem-repeat structures in C. elegans and other higher eukaryotes (Ellis et al. 1986). There are thought to be 100-150 copies of this repeat on chromosome I in C. elegans. The 5S rRNA genes are strikingly conserved between C. elegans and C. briggsae, with the genes in the two species identical in sequence (Butler et al. 1981; Nelson and Honda 1989). An estimated 100 copies of 5S rRNA lie in a tandem array on chromosome V in C. elegans.
###end p 93
###begin p 94
###xml 4 15 4 15 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 234 255 234 255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Nelson1">Nelson and Honda 1989</xref>
###xml 716 737 716 737 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Nelson1">Nelson and Honda 1989</xref>
###xml 4 15 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The C. briggsae rDNA repeat measured 7,429-7,431 bases with variations in length of a poly(A) tract and single nucleotides. The unit repeat contained one copy each of 5.8S, 28S, and 18S rDNA genes. In agreement with previous reports (Nelson and Honda 1989), two distinct 5S unit repeats were found of 697 bases and 938-940 bases. Each version contains a single copy of the 5S gene. Several minor variants of each version were apparent. Based on the number of reads present for each repeat, the rRNA array extends 410 kbp (55 copies), and the 5S arrays extend 20 kbp (30 copies) for the shorter unit and 70 kbp (70 copies) for the longer. The latter two estimates are in reasonable agreement with previous estimates (Nelson and Honda 1989).
###end p 94
###begin title 95
Spliced Leader RNA Genes
###end title 95
###begin p 96
###xml 25 35 25 35 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 63 68 63 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">trans</italic>
###xml 25 35 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
A characteristic of many C. elegans genes is the presence of a trans-spliced leader, a short RNA that is spliced onto the 5' end of the primary transcript prior to further processing. Two types of spliced leader, SL1 and SL2, have been described.
###end p 96
###begin p 97
###xml 4 7 4 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL1</italic>
###xml 100 121 100 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Nelson1">Nelson and Honda 1989</xref>
###xml 136 146 136 146 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 167 170 167 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL2</italic>
###xml 180 190 180 190 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 264 281 264 281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Evans1">Evans et al. 1997</xref>
###xml 333 344 333 344 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 360 363 360 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL2</italic>
###xml 436 439 436 439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL2</italic>
###xml 467 477 467 477 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 515 525 515 525 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 564 567 564 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL2</italic>
###xml 640 643 640 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL2</italic>
###xml 693 696 693 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SL2</italic>
###xml 136 146 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 180 190 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 333 344 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 467 477 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 515 525 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The SL1 RNA gene that donates the SL1 spliced leader is present on the 938 bp 5S rRNA repeat units (Nelson and Honda 1989), as it is in C. elegans. There are 18 known SL2 genes in C. elegans. They vary somewhat in sequence and are scattered throughout the genome (Evans et al. 1997; T. Blumenthal, unpublished data). We searched the C. briggsae genome for the SL2 RNA genes and found 18 matches. These matches encode four of the eleven SL2 sequence variants known in C. elegans as well as two variants not found in C. elegans. In both species, roughly half of the SL2 RNA genes are found in a few small clusters. A phylogenetic tree of the SL2 RNA genes in the two species indicates that four SL2 RNA genes in the last common ancestor expanded after separation of the species to create the 18-member gene families that exist today.
###end p 97
###begin title 98
MicroRNA Genes
###end title 98
###begin p 99
###xml 51 61 51 61 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 117 132 117 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Lau1">Lau et al. 2001</xref>
###xml 134 153 134 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Lee1">Lee and Ambros 2001</xref>
###xml 155 173 155 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Ambros1">Ambros et al. 2003</xref>
###xml 175 191 175 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Grad1">Grad et al. 2003</xref>
###xml 193 208 193 208 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Lim1">Lim et al. 2003</xref>
###xml 262 273 262 273 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 467 485 467 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Wuchty1">Wuchty et al. 1999</xref>
###xml 488 504 488 504 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Lim1">Lim et al. (2003</xref>
###xml 527 537 527 537 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 563 574 563 574 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 51 61 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 262 273 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 527 537 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 563 574 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The microRNA Registry (version 1.4; ) contains 105 C. elegans microRNA (miRNA) sequences reported by several groups (Lau et al. 2001; Lee and Ambros 2001; Ambros et al. 2003; Grad et al. 2003; Lim et al. 2003). We find close homologs of 70 of these genes in the C. briggsae genome, with greater than 90% sequence identity of the mature miRNA sequence and predicted ability of the flanking regions to form a precursor hairpin of around 70 nucleotides using ViennaRNA (Wuchty et al. 1999). Lim et al. (2003) report that 46 of 48 C. elegans miRNA families extend to C. briggsae using more relaxed sequence identity criteria.
###end p 99
###begin p 100
###xml 36 46 36 46 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 68 74 68 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mir-42</italic>
###xml 76 82 76 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mir-43</italic>
###xml 88 94 88 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mir-44</italic>
###xml 228 238 228 238 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 303 314 303 314 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 358 368 358 368 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 381 387 381 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mir-35</italic>
###xml 392 398 392 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mir-41</italic>
###xml 416 427 416 427 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 453 468 453 468 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Lau1">Lau et al. 2001</xref>
###xml 36 46 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 228 238 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 303 314 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 358 368 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 416 427 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Several miRNAs are clustered in the C. elegans genome (for example, mir-42, mir-43, and mir-44) and may be processed from the same primary transcript. Of nine clusters of two or more miRNA genes within regions of around 1 kb in C. elegans, we find seven with conserved gene order and orientation in the C. briggsae genome. An additional cluster contains six C. elegans paralogs to mir-35 and mir-41, versus eight in C. briggsae, as previously reported (Lau et al. 2001).
###end p 100
###begin title 101
Other ncRNA Genes
###end title 101
###begin p 102
###xml 65 76 65 76 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 177 187 177 187 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 65 76 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 177 187 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Our analysis identified 178 putative non-tRNA, non-rRNA genes in C. briggsae. The majority of classes, including U1, U2, U5, and SRP RNA, showed slightly higher copy numbers in C. elegans.
###end p 102
###begin p 103
###xml 31 41 31 41 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 45 56 45 56 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 136 146 136 146 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 266 277 266 277 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 348 358 348 358 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 443 454 443 454 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 31 41 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 45 56 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 136 146 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 266 277 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 348 358 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 443 454 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
The Rfam search failed to find C. elegans or C. briggsae RNAase P and U3 small nucleolar RNA (snoRNA) sequences. However, RNAase P from C. elegans has recently been identified by others (R. Klein, personal communication), and with aid of this sequence, the matching C. briggsae sequence was then easily found using BLASTN. BLASTN searches with six C. elegans U3 snoRNAs (T. Jones, personal communication) identified four matching genes in the C. briggsae genome.
###end p 103
###begin p 104
###xml 106 117 106 117 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 124 134 124 134 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 397 408 397 408 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 419 429 419 429 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 513 524 513 524 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 627 637 627 637 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 838 849 838 849 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 106 117 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 124 134 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 397 408 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 419 429 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 513 524 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 627 637 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 838 849 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
It is interesting to note that there are roughly twice as many putative U6 small nuclear RNAs (snRNAs) in C. briggsae as in C. elegans. Upon further examination, we found that the U6 Rfam family appears to contain large numbers of pseudogenes, and thus the observed expansion may reflect recent pseudogene duplication. The putative U6 snRNA sequences are remarkably conserved, with 22 clusters in C. briggsae and 16 in C. elegans having identical sequences. Two regions of around 10 kbp on the same FPC contig in C. briggsae (cb25.fpc2888) contain six and three U6 snRNA genes and correspond to two similar clusters located on C. elegans chromosome IV. Additional highly similar U6 hits can be found flanking these regions and in additional clusters. However, a neighbor-joining tree of all 63 putative U6 snRNAs did not show any obvious C. briggsae-specific subfamily expansion (data not shown).
###end p 104
###begin title 105
Missing ncRNA Genes
###end title 105
###begin p 106
###xml 91 102 91 102 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 168 178 168 178 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 275 286 275 286 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 290 300 290 300 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 91 102 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 168 178 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 275 286 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 290 300 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We found no homologs of the U12 spliceosome components U4atac, U6atac, U11, and U12 in the C. briggsae sequence. This spliceosome has not been previously identified in C. elegans or other nematodes. We found no obvious homologs of telomerase RNA or of several snoRNAs in the C. briggsae or C. elegans genomes, suggesting significant divergence from previously identified examples.
###end p 106
###begin title 107
Repetitive Elements
###end title 107
###begin p 108
###xml 38 50 38 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 127 144 127 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Bao1">Bao and Eddy 2002</xref>
###xml 411 421 411 421 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 38 49 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 411 421 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
To characterize the repeat content of C. briggsae, we applied RECON, an ab initio repetitive element identification algorithm (Bao and Eddy 2002) to identify repetitive sequences with more than ten copies in the genome. Putative repetitive elements were then screened to remove RNA and protein families not associated with transposable elements. For the purposes of comparison, we applied the same algorithm to C. elegans.
###end p 108
###begin p 109
###xml 34 45 34 45 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 107 117 107 117 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 197 208 197 208 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 223 241 223 241 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Harris1">Harris et al. 1990</xref>
###xml 253 271 253 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Prasad1">Prasad et al. 1991</xref>
###xml 277 288 277 288 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 301 311 301 311 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 353 381 353 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Plasterk1">Plasterk and von Luenen 1997</xref>
###xml 34 45 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 107 117 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 197 208 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 277 288 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 301 311 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The RECON-constructed library for C. briggsae contains 473 consensus repeat sequences, and the library for C. elegans contains 377. Previously reported transposons with more than ten copies in the C. briggsae genome, Tcb1 (Harris et al. 1990) and Tcb2 (Prasad et al. 1991) for C. briggsae, as well as C. elegans transposons Tc1, Tc2, Tc3, Tc6, and Tc7 (Plasterk and von Luenen 1997), were all recovered in the corresponding library.
###end p 109
###begin p 110
###xml 82 93 82 93 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 111 121 111 121 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 197 208 197 208 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 247 258 247 258 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 307 318 307 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans,</italic>
###xml 82 93 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 111 121 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 197 208 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 247 258 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 307 317 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
When the RECON libraries were used as the substrate to RepeatMasker, 22.4% of the C. briggsae and 16.5% of the C. elegans genomes were masked. Extrapolation to the expected 104 Mbp of the complete C. briggsae genome indicates that 23.3 Mbp of the C. briggsae genome is repetitive, as opposed to 16.5 Mbp of C. elegans, which has a contiguous genome size of 100.3 Mbp. Hence, the differential repeat content accounts almost entirely for the different observed sizes of the species' genomes.
###end p 110
###begin p 111
###xml 93 94 93 94 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">0</sub>
###xml 92 95 92 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c<sub>0</sub>t</italic>
###xml 170 192 170 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Britten1">Britten and Kohne 1968</xref>
###xml 199 210 199 210 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 237 247 237 247 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 266 276 266 276 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 303 314 303 314 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 370 390 370 390 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Arabidopsis thaliana</named-content>
###xml 459 469 459 469 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 493 504 493 504 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 199 210 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 237 247 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 266 276 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 303 314 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 370 390 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">Arabidopsis thaliana</span>
###xml 459 469 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 493 504 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Comparison of the repetitive portion of the two genomes confirms the early observation from c0t curves that closely related species contain similar repetitive sequences (Britten and Kohne 1968): the C. briggsae library masks 4.6% of the C. elegans genome, while the C. elegans library masks 6.6% of the C. briggsae genome. In contrast, the RECON-constructed library for Arabidopsis thaliana (Z. Bao and S. R. Eddy, unpublished data) can only mask 0.2% of the C. elegans genome and 0.1% of the C. briggsae genome.
###end p 111
###begin p 112
###xml 67 68 67 68 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio.0000045-t006">6</xref>
###xml 73 74 73 74 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio.0000045-t007">7</xref>
###xml 100 111 100 111 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 202 213 202 213 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 399 410 399 410 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 415 425 415 425 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 100 111 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 202 213 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 399 410 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 415 425 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The top ten repeat families in the two genomes are shown in Tables 6 and 7. Interestingly, a single C. briggsae repeat family, Cb000047, is present more than 20,000 times and constitutes 4.7 Mbp of the C. briggsae genome. In both genomes, the majority of repeat families are either short, nonautonomous DNA transposons or tandem arrays. The presence of Cb000047 is an interesting difference between C. briggsae and C. elegans, the largest of whose repeat families is present in roughly 3,000 copies.
###end p 112
###begin p 113
###xml 105 116 105 116 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 121 131 121 131 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 105 116 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 121 131 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Despite their general similarities, we were not able to systematically identify ortholog pairs among the C. briggsae and C. elegans repeats. When we used RepeatMasker to compare the sequences of one library against the other, we found no simple one-to-one mapping between them. Furthermore, similarity between repeat element pairs was generally restricted to subparts of the consensus sequences, presumably reflecting domains important for the propagation of the elements. It is not yet clear whether the overall similarity in repeat composition between the two genomes is due to orthology or because related genomes tend to be permissive for similar types of repeats (in particular, transposable elements). The relatively small amount of similarity between the repeat libraries in the two species suggests that most observed dispersed repeat elements postdate the divergence of the two species.
###end p 113
###begin title 114
###xml 23 34 23 34 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 39 49 39 49 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 23 34 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 39 49 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Genome Organization of C. briggsae and C. elegans
###end title 114
###begin p 115
###xml 44 55 44 55 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 60 70 60 70 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 184 204 184 204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Kent1">Kent and Zahler 2000</xref>
###xml 346 356 346 356 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 398 409 398 409 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 44 55 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 60 70 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 346 356 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 398 409 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
To begin to compare the organization of the C. briggsae and C. elegans genomes, we created whole-genome alignments of the two genomes at the nucleotide level using the WABA algorithm (Kent and Zahler 2000). WABA produced a total of 1,340,518 blocks of alignment. After adjusting for overlaps, the WABA alignments were found to cover 52.3% of the C. elegans genome (52.4/100.2 Mbp) and 50.1% of the C. briggsae assembly (52.9/105.6 Mbp).
###end p 115
###begin p 116
###xml 90 100 90 100 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 90 100 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
To characterize the alignments, we compared them with the positions of annotations on the C. elegans genome, using the WS77* annotations for the positions of genes, coding regions, and introns, and the WS87 annotations (October 2002) for the positions of 5' and 3' UTRs (the annotations for which were not available in WS77). In addition, we also scored aligned regions that fell within the upstream and downstream regions of genes, which were defined arbitrarily as the region 1,000 bp 5' to the translational initiation codon for upstream regions and the region 1,000 bp 3' of the translational stop codon for downstream regions.
###end p 116
###begin p 117
###xml 0 7 0 7 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio.0000045-t008">Table 8</xref>
###xml 92 102 92 102 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 92 102 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
