For each of these 338 trees, the branch lengths were re-estimated under the assumption of rate constancy, using Takezaki and Nei's (1995) program with the A correction for multiple hits. We calibrated the linearized trees by taking the nematode/arthropod divergence to be 800-1,000 MYA (Blaxter 1998).
###end p 228
###begin title 229
Gene family clustering
###end title 229
###begin p 230
###xml 62 77 62 77 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Van1">Van Dongen 2000</xref>
###xml 79 98 79 98 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Enright1">Enright et al. 2002</xref>
###xml 286 297 286 297 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 302 312 302 312 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 396 419 396 419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Smith1">Smith and Waterman 1981</xref>
###xml 421 433 421 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Pearson1">Pearson 1991</xref>
###xml 897 922 897 922 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Zdobnov1">Zdobnov and Apweiler 2001</xref>
###xml 938 957 938 957 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Bateman1">Bateman et al. 2002</xref>
###xml 1124 1134 1124 1134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="sd006">Dataset S6</xref>
###xml 286 297 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 302 312 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Gene families were identified utilizing the TRIBE-MCL method (Van Dongen 2000; Enright et al. 2002). Briefly, TRIBE-MCL identifies gene families using a Markov Clustering (MCL) procedure operating on a matrix of expectation values computed from a similarity search of all versus all of C. briggsae and C. elegans protein sequences. We used the Smith-Waterman algorithm as implemented in SSEARCH (Smith and Waterman 1981; Pearson 1991) to achieve a greater measure of sensitivity than BLASTP. The MCL clustering was executed with an inflation value of 1.6, chosen to minimize the number of orphaned or mispaired putative orthologs without greatly expanding the total number of clusters. Where more than one splice variant existed for a gene, only the longest transcript was chosen as a representative for the gene. TRIBE cluster annotation was created by merging the information from the InterPro (Zdobnov and Apweiler 2001) and Pfam 9.0 (Bateman et al. 2002) domains that occurred in at least two of the genes in a family. The full output from the TRIBE-MCL clustering and the Pfam domains for each cluster are available as Dataset S6.
###end p 230
###begin p 231
###xml 231 251 231 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Thompson1">Thompson et al. 1994</xref>
###xml 369 385 369 385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Felsenstein1">Felsenstein 1989</xref>
To develop a phylogenetic tree of the sra chemosensory receptor protein family, we combined chemosensory receptor genes belonging to the same Pfam subfamily from both species into a joint file that was then aligned using ClustalW (Thompson et al. 1994). The output file was fed into the PHYLIP package (programs used include: seqboot, protdist, neighbor, and consense; Felsenstein 1989) to generate a tree file. TreeView, part of the PHYLIP package, was used to visualize the family relationships.
###end p 231
###begin p 232
###xml 87 109 87 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 87 98 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 99 109 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
To identify phylogenetic-tree-based ortholog pairs of the sra protein family, we chose C. briggsae/C. elegans protein pairs that were each other's closest neighbors in greater than 900 of 1,000 bootstrap repetitions.
###end p 232
###begin p 233
Physical clustering of genes in a family along the chromosomes was tested by a permutation test counting the number of genes in a sliding window of 15 genes that are members of the same TRIBE family cluster. The average per window in each species was compared to the averages for 1,000 simulated genomes of randomly ordered genes. The maximum observed value for the shuffled genomes was always found to be smaller than the observed genome state, indicating that physical clustering of gene families is significantly nonrandom.
###end p 233
###begin title 234
Prediction of ncRNA genes
###end title 234
###begin p 235
###xml 55 73 55 73 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Lowe1">Lowe and Eddy 1997</xref>
###xml 275 286 275 286 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 308 328 308 328 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Altschul1">Altschul et al. 1997</xref>
###xml 498 499 498 499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 601 628 601 628 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Griffiths-Jones1">Griffiths-Jones et al. 2003</xref>
###xml 663 672 663 672 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Eddy1">Eddy 2002</xref>
###xml 275 286 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
We predicted tRNA genes using tRNAscan-SE version 123 (Lowe and Eddy 1997) in eukaryotic mode with default parameters and a threshold of 20 bits. To predict rRNA and miRNA genes, we extracted sequences from the sequence databases and searched for homologous sequences in the C. briggsae genome using BLASTN (Altschul et al. 1997). True matches were defined as those having greater than 95% identity over greater than 95% of the query length. Fragmentary matches were defined as all other hits with p value of <0.001. We predicted all other ncRNA genes using the Rfam 3.0 library of covariance models (Griffiths-Jones et al. 2003) and the INFERNAL software suite (Eddy 2002) with Rfam family-specific score thresholds.
###end p 235
###begin title 236
Repeat families
###end title 236
###begin p 237
###xml 115 127 115 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae.</italic>
###xml 218 229 218 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elegans.lib</italic>
###xml 258 268 258 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Jurka1">Jurka 2000</xref>
###xml 314 324 314 324 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 115 126 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 314 324 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We used RepeatMasker (A. F. A. Smit and P. Green, unpublished data) to identify presumptive repetitive elements in C. briggsae. Two different repeat library files were used to run RepeatMasker. The first library file, elegans.lib, was obtained from RepBase (Jurka 2000). RepBase includes all previously identified C. elegans repeat elements, as well as repeat elements from a variety of vertebrate and invertebrate species.
###end p 237
###begin p 238
###xml 5 16 5 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elegans.lib</italic>
###xml 70 81 70 81 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 134 151 134 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Bao1">Bao and Eddy 2002</xref>
###xml 650 666 650 666 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Morgenstern1">Morgenstern 1999</xref>
###xml 794 806 794 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae,</italic>
###xml 885 895 885 895 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 70 81 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 794 805 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 885 895 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
When elegans.lib failed to identify the expected number of repeats in C. briggsae, we built a second repeat library file using RECON (Bao and Eddy 2002). For the initial all versus all pairwise comparison of genomic sequences, the result of which serves as input to RECON, we used WUBLAST (W. R. Gish, unpublished data; ) with options "-kap E=0.00001 wordmask=dust wordmask=seg maskextra=20 -hspmax 5000 M=5 N=-11 Q=22 R=11." All parameters of RECON were left at their default values. For RECON-defined families with more than ten copies, a consensus sequence for each was constructed by aligning the ten longest members of the family with DIALIGN2 (Morgenstern 1999), with its default options, then selecting a simple majority rule consensus residue for each column in the multialignment. For C. briggsae, 723 consensuses were built. A total of 554 consensus sequences were built for C. elegans following the same protocol.
###end p 238
###begin p 239
###xml 225 235 225 235 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 240 251 240 251 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 323 333 323 333 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 338 349 338 349 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 463 472 463 472 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Eddy1">Eddy 2002</xref>
###xml 494 521 494 521 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Griffiths-Jones1">Griffiths-Jones et al. 2003</xref>
###xml 528 539 528 539 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 631 641 631 641 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 225 235 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 240 251 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 323 333 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 338 349 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 528 539 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 631 641 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
RECON has a known artifact in which it identifies conserved protein family domain and multicopy noncoding genes such as tRNAs and rRNAs in addition to finding bona fide repeat family elements. We removed these cases from the C. elegans and C. briggsae RECON library files by applying a series of filters. Before filtering, C. elegans and C. briggsae RECON library files contained 554 and 723 entries, respectively. To remove known ncRNA species, we ran INFERNAL (Eddy 2002) together with Rfam (Griffiths-Jones et al. 2003). For C. briggsae, this step removed 22 tRNAs, two histone H3 genes, and one each of U1, U2, U5, and U6. For C. elegans, this step removed 20 tRNAs, three rRNAs, one histone H3 gene, and one each of U1, U2, U5, and U6.
###end p 239
###begin p 240
###xml 174 185 174 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elegans.lib</italic>
###xml 293 303 293 303 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 359 370 359 370 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 392 412 392 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Altschul1">Altschul et al. 1997</xref>
###xml 492 502 492 502 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 507 518 507 518 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 614 616 614 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E-</italic>
###xml 625 628 625 628 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;30</sup>
###xml 644 654 644 654 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 677 687 677 687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Jurka1">Jurka 2000</xref>
###xml 739 741 739 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E-</italic>
###xml 750 753 750 753 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;10</sup>
###xml 833 843 833 843 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 874 884 874 884 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 921 932 921 932 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 293 303 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 359 370 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 492 502 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 507 518 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 644 654 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 833 843 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 874 884 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 921 932 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Prior to removing gene family domains from the RECON libraries, it was necessary to remove transposons and other repetitive gene calls from the gene prediction sets. We used elegans.lib to identify "trusted repeats" in the RECON libraries, finding 188 trusted repeats in the RECON library for C. elegans and 72 trusted repeats in the RECON repeat library for C. briggsae. We then used BLAST (Altschul et al. 1997) to identify and remove trusted repeat sequences from the DNA sequences of the C. elegans and C. briggsae gene sets. A gene prediction was taken to be a transposable element if it had a TBLASTN hit of E-value <10-30 in the RepBase C. elegans library (version 8.2; Jurka 2000) or if its individual exons all had BLASTN hits of E-value <10-10 in the RECON repeat library for that species. This step removed 303 genes from C. elegans WS77 gene set, 434 genes from C. elegans hybrid gene set, and 627 genes from C. briggsae gene set.
###end p 240
###begin p 241
###xml 99 109 99 109 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 114 125 114 125 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 226 227 226 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E</italic>
###xml 237 240 237 240 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;10</sup>
###xml 295 305 295 305 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 310 321 310 321 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 506 517 506 517 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 577 587 577 587 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 99 109 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 114 125 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 295 305 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 310 321 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 506 517 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 577 587 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We next used TBLASTN to match the library of RECON-identified repeat elements against the filtered C. elegans and C. briggsae hybrid gene sets as well as SwissProt, and we removed repeat families that matched proteins with an E-value <10-10. A total of 181 and 382 entries were removed from the C. elegans and C. briggsae RECON libraries, respectively. Finally, we manually examined those repeat entries with significant protein hits and added an additional eight entries to the trusted repeat library for C. briggsae. Manual examination did not yield more trusted repeats for C. elegans.
###end p 241
###begin p 242
###xml 49 60 49 60 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 69 79 69 79 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 49 60 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 69 79 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The final filtered RECON libraries contained 473 C. briggsae and 377 C. elegans entries.
###end p 242
###begin p 243
###xml 39 49 39 49 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="sd007">Dataset S7</xref>
The repeat family data can be found as Dataset S7.
###end p 243
###begin title 244
Nucleotide-level sequence alignments
###end title 244
###begin p 245
###xml 63 74 63 74 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 104 114 104 114 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 221 231 221 231 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 63 74 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 104 114 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 221 231 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We used the WABA algorithm (Kent and Zahler 2002) to align the C. briggsae WGS assembly to the complete C. elegans genomic sequence. All WGS supercontigs were "cut" into 100 kbp pieces and individually aligned to the six C. elegans chromosomes. The coordinates of the regions of alignment were then transformed back into supercontig coordinates for further analysis.
###end p 245
###begin p 246
###xml 63 73 63 73 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 63 73 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
To characterize raw WABA aligning segments, we partitioned the C. elegans genome into eight compartments corresponding to CDS, introns, 5' and 3' UTRs, upstream regions, downstream regions, and repeat regions. The remainder of the genome was considered to be intergenic. For consistency, upstream regions were considered to be 1,000 bp upstream of the translational start site, and downstream regions were considered to be 1,000 bp downstream of the translational stop, regardless of whether or not the UTRs of the gene were known. In the case of a region that could be scored in two or more ways, such as a region that is within the 1,000 bp downstream window of one gene and upstream of another, the region was assigned to one partition on the basis of left-to-right priority in the list above. For example, CDSs have priority over an intron. A WABA segment was scored as belonging to a partition if it shared at least one base overlap with a region in that partition.
###end p 246
###begin p 247
For the purposes of comparison, we also repeated the whole-genome alignment with the BLASTZ algorithm (Schwarz et al. 2003). The results were highly comparable, but the coverage was slightly lower with BLASTZ (56% coverage with BLASTZ versus 65% coverage with WABA, not adjusted for overlaps).
###end p 247
###begin title 248
Synteny block construction
###end title 248
###begin p 249
###xml 309 319 309 319 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 353 364 353 364 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 564 574 564 574 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 579 590 579 590 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 309 319 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 353 364 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 564 574 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 579 590 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
To identify putative syntenic regions from the raw WABA alignment blocks, we merged adjacent "strong," "weak," and "coding" blocks into a smaller number of contiguous blocks. This reduced the 1.3 million raw WABA blocks to 104,097 contiguous blocks. From this set, we discarded blocks in which more than five C. elegans segments aligned to a segment of C. briggsae or vice versa. The remaining alignments were merged using the "simple merge" algorithm, which searches for and merges uninterrupted series of alignments that are monotonically increasing in both the C. elegans and C. briggsae genomes. This procedure yielded 26,231 merged blocks of alignment.
###end p 249
###begin p 250
###xml 260 271 260 271 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 719 729 719 729 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 733 744 733 744 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 260 271 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 719 729 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 733 744 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
We then performed an additional round of merging using a dynamic programming algorithm to identify the longest monotonically increasing set of alignment blocks. Unlike the simple merge, this algorithm can jump over interrupted regions of colinearity. For each C. briggsae supercontig, the algorithm first finds the longest series of blocks then finds the next longest series using those left over from the first iteration. This continues until no blocks remain. During the process, the identification of monotonically increasing blocks is constrained so that no gap in the series can be greater than 100 kbp in either genome and so that no single gap can cause a relative expansion of greater than 5-fold in either the C. elegans or C. briggsae coordinates. This step yielded 13,467 merged blocks.
###end p 250
###begin p 251
###xml 444 454 444 454 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 444 454 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Examination of the distribution of synteny block lengths showed a large asymmetric peak at 1,250 bp and a long tail of longer block lengths (data not shown). Most of these blocks involved a single unmerged WABA alignment and correlated poorly with the positions of previously identified orthologs. To exclude these small blocks from further analysis, we filtered the blocks for a lower size limit of 1,850 bp, which reduced the coverage of the C. elegans genome by 1.5% but excluded 64% of the merged blocks, leaving a final candidate list of 4,837 synteny blocks.
###end p 251
###begin p 252
###xml 124 127 124 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a/b</italic>
###xml 132 135 132 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c/d</italic>
###xml 139 151 139 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae:</italic>
###xml 139 150 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Each block was classified as an inversion, transposition, or reciprocal translocation by examining the breakpoint junctions a/b and c/d in C. briggsae:
###end p 252
###begin p 253
###xml 42 43 42 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 60 61 60 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c</italic>
###xml 66 67 66 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</italic>
###xml 84 85 84 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</italic>
###xml 110 120 110 120 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 179 180 179 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 185 186 185 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</italic>
###xml 204 214 204 214 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 384 385 384 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 402 403 402 403 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">f</italic>
###xml 407 408 407 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">e</italic>
###xml 425 426 425 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">d</italic>
###xml 430 441 430 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans.</italic>
###xml 110 120 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 204 214 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 430 440 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
A block was classified as an inversion if a was adjacent to c and b was adjacent to d from the perspective of C. elegans coordinates. A block was classified as a transposition if a and d were adjacent in C. elegans and a reciprocal event could not be identified. A block was classified as involving one or two reciprocal translocations if another breakpoint  could be found such that a was adjacent to f or e was adjacent to d in C. elegans.
###end p 253
###begin title 254
###xml 13 23 13 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 13 23 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Updating the C. elegans gene set
###end title 254
###begin p 255
###xml 26 46 26 46 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio.0000045-Altschul1">Altschul et al. 1997</xref>
###xml 55 66 55 66 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 133 143 133 143 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 210 221 210 221 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 443 453 443 453 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 598 600 598 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E-</italic>
###xml 609 611 609 611 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;3</sup>
###xml 619 630 619 630 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 715 725 715 725 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 885 887 885 887 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;3</sup>
###xml 895 906 895 906 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 1010 1020 1010 1020 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 1205 1207 1205 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E-</italic>
###xml 1303 1313 1303 1313 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 1502 1504 1502 1504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E-</italic>
###xml 55 66 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 133 143 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 210 221 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 443 453 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 619 630 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 715 725 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 895 906 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 1010 1020 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1303 1313 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We used TBLASTN searches (Altschul et al. 1997) of the C. briggsae genome to see how many of the gene model changes suggested in the C. elegans hybrid gene set, compared to the WS77 gene set, were supported by C. briggsae similarity. We only considered new hybrid exons and extensions and truncations or deletions of existing WS77 exons where the extended or truncated region was greater than or equal to five amino acids (15 bp) long. If the C. elegans hybrid gene set predicted a new exon in an existing WS77 gene, we considered the new exon to be well-supported if the exon had a TBLASTN hit of E-value <10-3 in the C. briggsae genome that covered greater than or equal to 10 amino acids of the new exon. If the C. elegans hybrid gene set predicted an extension of an existing WS77 exon, we considered the extension to be well-supported if the extended exon had a TBLASTN hit of <10-3 in the C. briggsae genome which covered greater than or equal to 10 amino acids of the extended part. In contrast, if the C. elegans hybrid gene set predicted that an existing exon in a WS77 gene should be deleted, we considered the exon deletion to be well supported if the WS77 exon did not have any TBLASTN hit of E-value <0.1 that covered greater than or equal to five amino acids of the exon. Likewise, if the C. elegans hybrid gene set predicted that an existing exon in a WS77 gene should be truncated, we considered the exon truncation to be well-supported if the WS77 exon did not have any TBLASTN hit of E-value <0.1 that covered greater than ot equal to five amino acids of the truncated part.
###end p 255

###xml 23 46 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">Caenorhabditis briggsae</span>
The Genome Sequence of Caenorhabditis briggsae: A Platform for Comparative Genomics
###end p 284
###begin p 285
###xml 14 25 14 25 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 30 40 30 40 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 242 253 242 253 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 258 268 258 268 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 411 421 411 421 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 14 25 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 30 40 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 96 101 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 107 112 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 242 253 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 258 268 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 411 421 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The nematodes C. briggsae and C. elegans diverged 80-110 MYA, near to the time of divergence of human from mouse, but are almost indistinguishable morphologically. These figures demonstrate the high degree of morphological similarity between C. briggsae and C. elegans and show how the patterns of evolutionary conservation between the two species vary across the five autosomes (I-V) and sex chromosome (X) of C. elegans.

###end p 289
###begin p 290
###xml 201 215 201 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis</italic>

###xml 322 332 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We thank Hugh Robertson for helpful discussions on the chemosensory receptor families and Paul Sternberg, Karin Kiontke, and Marie-Anne Felix for their insights into the anatomic differences among the Caenorhabditis species. We are grateful to Sean Eddy, Tom Jones, and Robbie Klein for providing us with the sequences of C. elegans RNAase P and U3 snoRNA. We thank David Baillie for discussions on the repetitive elements and for pointing us to key references. We thank Paula Kassos for proofreading the manuscript. We also are grateful to the three anonymous reviewers who reviewed this paper.

###xml 60 65 60 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acy-4</italic>
###xml 20 30 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 35 46 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
Joint Refinement of C. elegans and C. briggsae Gene Models: acy-4
###end title 448
###begin p 449
###xml 20 31 20 31 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 36 52 36 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans acy-4</italic>
###xml 88 96 88 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ce-acy-4</italic>
###xml 127 135 127 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cb-acy-4</italic>
###xml 197 208 197 208 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>
###xml 215 225 215 225 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 332 340 332 340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cb-acy-4</italic>
###xml 345 353 345 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ce-acy-4</italic>
###xml 436 444 436 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ce-acy-4</italic>
###xml 472 479 472 479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T01C2.1</italic>
###xml 490 498 490 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ce-acy-4</italic>
###xml 20 31 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 36 46 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 197 208 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 215 225 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
When annotating the C. briggsae and C. elegans acy-4 orthologs, we chose the Genefinder ce-acy-4 prediction and the Genefinder cb-acy-4 prediction because, out of the 12 possible combinations of a C. briggsae and a C. elegans prediction, this pair shows the most similarity to each other. Coding sequence (CDS) conservation between cb-acy-4 and ce-acy-4 provides evidence for as many as 12 additional N-terminal exons in the Genefinder ce-acy-4 prediction, as compared to T01C2.1, the WS77 ce-acy-4 prediction. Subsequently, four of the additional N-terminal exons that were predicted by FGENESH and Genefinder were confirmed by new EST data (marked with asterisks).
###end p 449

###begin p 460
###xml 4 14 4 14 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>

###xml 4 14 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
(B) C. elegans gene density and genetic map position. Gene density is plotted as a histogram, showing a relatively uniform distribution of genes across each chromosome. The relationship of the position of genes on the genetic map to their position on the sequence is superimposed on the y-axis. Steeper slopes in this plot indicate higher rates of meiotic recombination. Inflection points in the genetic map plot reflect the division of the chromosomes into recombinationally active "arms" and recombinationally slow "centers."
###end p 460
###begin p 461
###xml 4 26 4 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. briggsae/C. elegans</italic>
###xml 4 15 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>
###xml 16 26 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>

###begin p 462
###xml 4 14 4 14 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 74 85 74 85 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. briggsae</named-content>

###xml 74 85 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">C. briggsae</span>

(D) C. elegans "orphans," genes with no significant protein similarity in C. briggsae or the non-C. elegans portion of SwissProt. This histogram has been normalized for gene density in 100 kbp sliding windows. Spikes in orphan density seem to correlate with regions of low ortholog density.
###end p 462
###begin p 463
###xml 4 14 4 14 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>
###xml 4 14 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
(E) C. elegans genes that mutate to lethality or are lethal in RNAi screens, in 100 kbp sliding windows normalized to overall gene density. This track shows the distribution of essential genes and demonstrates their tendency to cluster in the chromosome centers.
###end p 463
###begin p 464
(F) Repetitive elements, binned in 100 kbp sliding windows. Repeat-rich regions correlate with both the absence of significant syntenic coverage and ortholog-poor regions.
###end p 464
###begin p 465
###xml 9 10 9 10 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</sub>

(G) The KA/KS ratio in ortholog pairs. Lower values indicate greater levels of purifying selection.

###begin p 466

Updating the C. elegans Gene Set Using C. briggsae Similarity
###end title 489
###begin p 490
###xml 44 54 44 54 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">C. elegans</named-content>

###xml 44 54 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 238 248 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We have catalogued possible improvements to C. elegans gene models, for both the WS77 gene set used in this paper and also for the more recent WS103 gene set (June 2003). For WS103, we only have catalogued possible changes for the 15,943 C. elegans WS103 gene models that did not change between WS77 and WS103
